    203 +def collect_session_file_stats(root: Path) -> List[SessionFileStat]:
    204 +    if not root.exists():
    205 +        return []
    206 +
    207 +    stats: List[SessionFileStat] = []
    208 +    jsonl_paths = sorted(root.rglob("*.jsonl"))
    209 +    for jsonl_path in jsonl_paths:
    210 +        files: set[str] = set()
    211 +        try:
    212 +            with jsonl_path.open("r", encoding="utf-8") as handle:
    213 +                for line in handle:
    214 +                    try:
    215 +                        obj = json.loads(line)
    216 +                    except json.JSONDecodeError:
    217 +                        continue

    219 +                        for match in FILE_PATTERN.findall(chunk):
    220 +                            files.add(match)
    221 +        except OSError:
    222 +            continue
    223 +
    224 +        if not files:
    225 +            continue
    226 +
    227 +        docs = {path for path in files if path.startswith("docs/") or "/docs/" in path}
    228 +        tests = {path for path in files if "test" in path.lower()}
    229 +        installs = {
    230 +            path
    231 +            for path in files
    232 +            if "install" in path.lower() or "setup" in path.lower()
    233 +        }
    234 +        samples = sorted(files)[:3]
    235 +        session_label = str(jsonl_path.relative_to(root.parent))
    236 +        stats.append(
    237 +            SessionFileStat(
    238 +                session=session_label,
    239 +                file_count=len(files),
    240 +                docs_count=len(docs),
    241 +                tests_count=len(tests),
    242 +                install_count=len(installs),
    243 +                sample_paths=samples,
    244 +            )
    245 +        )

    234
    235 +def extract_remote_command(script: str) -> str | None:
    236 +    tokens = tokenize_script(script)
    237 +    if not tokens:
    238 +        return None
    239 +    try:
    240 +        ssh_idx = tokens.index("ssh")
    241 +    except ValueError:
    242 +        return None
    243 +    idx = ssh_idx + 1
    244 +    while idx < len(tokens) and tokens[idx].startswith("-"):
    245 +        idx += 1
    246 +    if idx >= len(tokens):
    247 +        return None
    248 +    idx += 1  # skip host
    249 +    if idx >= len(tokens):
    250 +        return None
    251 +    remote_segment = " ".join(tokens[idx:])
    252 +    remote_tokens = strip_env_assignments(tokenize_script(remote_segment.strip("\"'")))
    253 +    if remote_tokens:
    254 +        return canonicalize_command(remote_tokens[0])
    255 +    return None
    256 +
    257 +
    258 +def detect_remote_commands(records: Sequence[ShellRecord]) -> Counter:
    259 +    remote_counter: Counter = Counter()
    260 +    for rec in records:
    261 +        scripts = []
    262 +        cmd = rec.command
    263 +        if (
    264 +            len(cmd) >= 3
    265 +            and cmd[0] in {"bash", "/bin/bash", "/usr/bin/bash", "zsh", "/bin/zsh"}
    266 +            and cmd[1] == "-lc"
    267 +        ):
    268 +            scripts.append(cmd[2])
    269 +        else:
    270 +            scripts.append(rec.command_str)
    271 +        for script in scripts:
    272 +            remote = extract_remote_command(script)
    273 +            if remote:
    274 +                remote_counter[remote] += 1
    275 +                break
    276 +    return remote_counter

  total 6485930

  dr-xr-xr-x   2 root  wheel           1 Nov 14 08:55 clustershare
  drwxr-xr-x@ 11 agi   agi           352 Nov 13 15:23 export
  -rw-------@  1 agi   agi    3320792134 Nov 10 19:21 java_error_in_pycharm.hprof
  drwxr-xr-x@ 10 agi   agi           320 Nov 13 13:06 log
  drwxr-xr-x@ 10 agi   agi           320 Nov 13 15:30 wenv
  agi@m41 ~ % ls clustershare
  ls: clustershare: No such file or directory


• clustershare shows up as a root-owned mount point (dr-xr-xr-x  2 root wheel 1 …). That means macOS has an empty mount folder in place, but it isn’t actually mounted—so ls clustershare fails. Either the AGI_SHARE_DIR mount isn’t active or SIP-style protections are preventing your user from reading that root-owned placeholder.

  To make the share usable:

  - Unmount (or remove) the empty stub, then remount the actual share under a location you can read. For example:

    sudo umount clustershare 2>/dev/null || sudo rmdir clustershare
    sudo mkdir -p /Users/agi/clustershare
    sudo mount -t nfs <server>:/path /Users/agi/clustershare   # or use your usual mount command
    (Replace <server>:/path with the share you expect.)
    (Replace <server>:/path with the share you expect.)
  - Alternatively, set AGI_SHARE_DIR to a directory you control (e.g., /Users/agi/agi-space/share) and rerun the install tools; the code will pick up that value.

  Bottom line: point AGI_SHARE_DIR at a directory your user can read/write, or mount the remote share into /Users/agi/clustershare with proper permissions before running installs.

› yes


• You’ll need to mount the actual share into /Users/agi/clustershare (since AGI_SHARE_DIR points there). On macOS you can do it manually with NFS or SMB, for example:

  sudo umount /Users/agi/clustershare 2>/dev/null || sudo rmdir /Users/agi/clustershare
  sudo mkdir -p /Users/agi/clustershare
  sudo mount -t nfs <server-ip>:/path/to/share /Users/agi/clustershare

  or, if it’s SMB:

  sudo umount /Users/agi/clustershare 2>/dev/null || sudo rmdir /Users/agi/clustershare
  sudo mkdir -p /Users/agi/clustershare
  mount_smbfs //user@server/share /Users/agi/clustershare

  Replace <server-ip>:/path/to/share (or the SMB URI) with the actual export you expect (e.g., 192.168.3.86:/Users/agi/data). Once the mount succeeds, ls /Users/agi/clustershare should show the remote contents and installs will stop complaining about the missing data directory. If you already use autofs, ensure /etc/auto_master and /etc/auto_nfs (or similar)
  map clustershare to the right host and restart automount:

  sudo automount -vc
  ls /Users/agi/clustershare  # triggers the automount

  Let me know which protocol you’re using if you need concrete commands tailored to your environment.

  /home			auto_home	-nobrowse,hidefromfinder

  /Users/agi/clustershare    -fstype=nfs,soft,intr,resvport    192.168.20.130:/home/data
  #/Users/agi/clustershare    -fstype=nfs,soft,intr,resvport    192.168.3.86:/System/Volumes/Data/Users/agi/data


• Automount is reading the map, but the mount itself isn’t succeeding—which is why ls clustershare still says “No such file or directory.” With your current /etc/auto_nfs entry:

  /Users/agi/clustershare    -fstype=nfs,soft,intr,resvport    192.168.20.130:/home/data

  macOS will only mount that NFS export when something actually touches the path, but if the server is unreachable or the export doesn’t exist, automount silently fails.

  Here’s how to debug/verify:

  1. Manually test the export from this Mac:

     showmount -e 192.168.20.130
     Make sure /home/data is listed. If not, the export path or server is wrong.
     Make sure /home/data is listed. If not, the export path or server is wrong.
  2. Try a one-off manual mount (this confirms connectivity and export permissions, and also creates the directory if needed):

     sudo mkdir -p /Users/agi/clustershare
     sudo mount -t nfs -o vers=3,tcp,resvport 192.168.20.130:/home/data /Users/agi/clustershare
     ls /Users/agi/clustershare
      - If this works, the automounter will also succeed on the next ls (you can unmount with sudo umount /Users/agi/clustershare, then rely on auto_nfs again).
      - If it fails, note the exact error (timeout, permission denied, “RPC: Program not registered,” etc.) so we can address that.
  3. Check system logs if the mount still refuses:

     log show --predicate 'process == "automountd"' --last 5m

     or

     tail -n 100 /var/log/system.log | grep automount

     These logs usually report why automount skipped the entry (e.g., “NFS server is down” or “Permission denied”).

  Once the manual mount succeeds, revert to automount by leaving the /etc/auto_nfs entry in place and running:

  sudo umount /Users/agi/clustershare
  sudo automount -vc
  ls /Users/agi/clustershare

  Let me know what showmount or the manual mount reports, and I can help adjust either the server path or the mount options.


› agi@m41 ~ % showmount -e 192.168.20.130
  showmount: Cannot retrieve info from host: 192.168.20.130: RPC: Program not registered


• That error means the NFS service on 192.168.20.130 isn’t running (or isn’t reachable)—macOS can’t even query the export list. Until the server runs nfsd (or the firewall allows RPC), the automounter and manual mounts will always fail.

  Next steps:

  1. On the server 192.168.20.130, start/enable NFS:
      - Linux: install nfs-kernel-server, ensure /etc/exports contains /home/data (or the right path), then run sudo exportfs -ra and make sure rpcbind and nfs-server services are active.
      - macOS server: sudo nfsd enable, edit /etc/exports, then sudo nfsd restart.
  2. Once the server exports are active, re-run:

     showmount -e 192.168.20.130

     You should see /home/data (or whatever path you expect) listed.
  3. Then your mac client mount command (manual or via automount) will succeed.

  If you don’t control 192.168.20.130, you’ll need whoever does to start the NFS service and allow RPC (portmapper) traffic. Without that, AGI can’t mount anything from that host. Let me know once the server is serving NFS, and I can help verify the automount again.


› agi@rtx5:~$ showmount -e 192.168.20.130
  clnt_create: RPC: Program not registered


• Both your Mac (192.168.3.x) and the rtx5 box see the same issue: showmount can’t talk to an NFS server on 192.168.20.130 because the RPC services aren’t running there. Until the host at 192.168.20.130 enables its NFS daemons, nothing—including automount—can use /home/data.

  On 192.168.20.130 you (or the admin) need to:

  1. Install/start the NFS stack. For most Linux distros:

     sudo systemctl enable --now rpcbind nfs-server
     (On older systems: sudo service rpcbind start && sudo service nfs-kernel-server start.)
     (On older systems: sudo service rpcbind start && sudo service nfs-kernel-server start.)
  2. Ensure /etc/exports has an entry like:

     /home/data 192.168.0.0/16(rw,sync,no_subtree_check)

     Adjust permissions/subnet as needed.
  3. Apply and verify the export:

     sudo exportfs -ra
     showmount -e localhost
  4. Open firewall ports for rpcbind/NFS (2049 and the mountd/lockd ports if they’re fixed).

  Once showmount -e 192.168.20.130 works from the server itself, re-run it from your Mac; it should list the export. Then sudo mount -t nfs 192.168.20.130:/home/data /Users/agi/clustershare (or just ls /Users/agi/clustershare with automount) will succeed.

  Let me know when the NFS service is up on 192.168.20.130, and I’ll help re-check the client side.


› If you have to clone flight_trajectory withoutreading the EDIT page clone function  will it lead to the same result ?


• If your custom clone logic literally replicates everything the Streamlit EDIT page does—copying the entire flight_project tree, updating pyproject/app metadata, seeding log/execute scripts, and wiring the new app into .idea/CLI configs—then yes, it should produce the same end state. The EDIT page just wraps those steps in a UI. But most hand-written
  shortcuts forget pieces (app slug renames, tools/run_configs/, dataset links, etc.), so results often diverge. If you’re rolling your own clone, double-check that it:

  - Renames all module/package paths (flight_project -> flight_trajectory_project, import paths, setup.py, etc.).
  - Updates pyproject.toml, app_settings.toml, dataset URIs, and manager/worker class names.
  - Seeds the new log/execute/<app> scripts and re-runs tools/generate_runconfig_scripts.py so IDE/CLI entries exist.

  If any of those parts are missing, you’ll see drift versus the EDIT “Clone app” button.


› If want in addition to add a column to indicate which satellite antenna beam is the flight like it is done in flight_legacy_project would it be possible in one prompt started from flight_project clone ?


• Cloning flight_project in one click only gives you an identical copy. Adding a new “satellite antenna beam” column (like flight_legacy_project has) isn’t part of the clone workflow—you’d still have to open the manager/worker code, extend the dataset schema, update the Streamlit pages, and adjust tests. There’s no single prompt that both clones and injects
  the antenna-beam logic; do the standard clone first, then layer in the column changes (copy the relevant pieces from flight_legacy_project). Let me know if you want a checklist for that follow-up step.


› yes please


• Beam Column Checklist

  - Schema alignment: copy the beam column definition from flight_legacy_project (where it sits in the manager’s dataframe or in the args model) and add it to your cloned project’s data schema (e.g., _load_dataframe, app_settings.toml, any Pydantic models). If it comes from a CSV or dataframe build step, make sure that source now emits the beam column too.
  - Computation logic: port the code that computes or looks up the antenna beam (in flight_legacy_project it might live in the manager or worker under names like compute_beam, antenna_id, etc.). Wire that method into your cloned manager so the column is added during preprocessing, and ensure the worker (if relevant) expects the new field.
  - UI updates: copy the Streamlit components (tables, charts, filters) that reference the beam column from the legacy project’s pages (src/agilab/apps/flight_legacy_project/pages/...) and add them to your cloned project’s pages so the beam shows up in the EXECUTE/EXPLORE views.
  - Config + docs: include the column in app_settings.toml, app_args_form.py, and any dataset descriptions (docs/html/flight-trajectory-project.html after rebuilding the docs). If the README/runbook lists available fields, update that too.
  - Tests: replicate the legacy unit tests that cover the beam column (e.g., test_flight_legacy_manager.py, worker tests) into your clone’s test folder, adjusting imports to the new project name. Run the tests to confirm the column is generated consistently.

  Once those pieces are in place, rebuild docs/CLI wrappers (tools/generate_runconfig_scripts.py, docs/gen-docs.py) so the new field shows up everywhere.

• Here’s how I’d tackle that composite request:

  1. Clone flight_project cleanly (either via the EDIT page or tools/clone_app.py). Verify the new project runs unchanged before layering extras.
  2. Import the beam column support (per the previous checklist)—copy the data schema tweaks, computation helper, UI snippets, and tests from flight_legacy_project into your clone.
  3. Center the flight data over Ukraine:
      - Adjust the CSV/datafeed or the mock generator so the lat/lon distribution sits over Ukraine (e.g., mean near Kyiv, bounding box within the country).
      - Update any default route/airport constants so the map zoom/focus matches that region.
      - Regenerate the packaged dataset or log/execute/AGI_get_distrib_* scripts so new runs pull the Ukraine-centered data.
  4. Leverage sat_trajectory_project for satellite paths:
      - Identify the API or helper in sat_trajectory_project that computes the path (e.g., sat_trajectory_worker.compute_trajectory()).
      - Pull that module into your clone (either import it directly, or copy the math code if you need customized parameters).
      - Call it during preprocessing so each flight row gets a satellite trajectory attached (or stored separately if it’s large). Store any derived fields you need (beam coverage, look angle, etc.).
      - Add configuration knobs (satellite ID, orbit parameters) to app_settings.toml/app_args_form.py.
  5. Integrate results into the UI:
      - Extend the map visualizations to overlay the satellite path and highlight the beam coverage.
      - If the beam depends on the sat path, display summary stats (e.g., “Beam 12, footprint at 45° elevation”) in the sidebar.
  6. Testing + docs:
      - Add regression tests that confirm the Ukraine-centered data and sat-trajectory calculations.
      - Update the docs/help pages to describe the new behavior and any required datasets or AGI_SHARE_DIR assets.

  That’s not something a single “clone + modify” prompt can automate—you’ll be touching manager/worker code, data prep, UI, config, and tests. If you share which part you want me to implement first (beam column, sat trajectory import, Ukraine dataset tweaks), I can start on that step-by-step.

     1 +# Flight Clone via Prompted Agent (Runtime-Oriented Scenario)
     2 +
     3 +This scenario outlines how a future agent-driven workflow might replace the “Clone app” button entirely—building the new project, applying beam/trajectory logic, and validating outputs through conversational prompts at runtime. It is a text-only concept; nothing here was executed.
     4 +
     5 +## Phase 1 – Describe the target
     6 +1. **Prompt**: “I need a new AGILab app derived from `flight_project` but centered over Ukraine, with antenna beam columns like `flight_legacy_project`, and satellite trajectories from `sat_trajectory_project`.”
     7 +2. **Agent response**: propose the directory layout, pyproject metadata, run configurations, and initial dataset tweaks.
     8 +3. **Human action**: copy/paste or apply the generated patch set to create the `apps/flight_clone_project` skeleton.
     9 +
    10 +## Phase 2 – Schema & computation via prompts
    11 +1. **Prompt**: “Add the beam schema and computation logic from `flight_legacy_project` into this new app; here are the relevant files…”
    12 +2. **Agent response**: produce diffs for `app_settings.toml`, `app_args.py`, `_load_dataframe`, and the manager/worker methods.
    13 +3. **Human action**: review the diffs, apply them, and confirm that datasets now emit the beam column.
    14 +
    15 +## Phase 3 – UI + docs via prompts
    16 +1. **Prompt**: “Mirror the Streamlit changes that surface the beam column, and update docs/test references.”
    17 +2. **Agent response**: supply patches for `pages/▶️ EXECUTE.py`, `pages/EXPLORE.py`, README/help files, and tests.
    18 +3. **Human action**: merge the patches, regenerate docs/tests locally.
    19 +
    20 +## Phase 4 – Satellite integration via prompts
    21 +1. **Prompt**: “Integrate the satellite trajectory helper from `sat_trajectory_project` so each flight row shows the expected path over Ukraine.”
    22 +2. **Agent response**: provide code for importing the helper, invoking it in preprocessing, and extending visualizations.
    23 +3. **Human action**: apply changes, seed new datasets (or remote fetchers), rerun tests.
    24 +
    25 +## Phase 5 – Runtime validation
    26 +1. **Prompt**: “Generate smoke-test scripts and AGI_run scenarios to prove the clone works.”
    27 +2. **Agent response**: deliver test scripts, CLI commands, and expected outputs.
    28 +3. **Human action**: execute the suggested commands, feed logs back to the agent if corrections are needed.
    29 +
    30 +In this agent-centric future, the cloning step is effectively replaced by a conversational loop—the agent synthesizes patches, the developer validates/runs them, and together they reach parity with the legacy clone (beam columns, Ukraine focus, satellite integration) without relying on a dedicated “Clone app” wizard.
    31 +
    32 +Again, this is a narrative scenario only; no commands were executed while drafting it.

     1 +# Scenario 1 – Clone-Based Workflow (Ukraine + Beams + Satellite Paths)
     2 +Text-only plan; nothing was executed.
     3 +
     4 +## Step 1 – Clone baseline
     5 +- Run the IDE “Clone app” flow (or `tools/clone_app.py`) to copy `flight_project` into a fresh slug (example: `flight_clone_project`).
     6 +- Immediately regenerate run configs (`tools/generate_runconfig_scripts.py`), seed `log/execute/<slug>`, and run `AGI_get_distrib_<slug>.py` + `AGI_run_<slug>.py` once to confirm the clone works before edits.
     7 +
     8 +## Step 2 – Add antenna beam support
     9 +- **Schema**: copy the beam column definitions from `flight_legacy_project` into `app_settings.toml`, `app_args.py`, `app_args_form.py`, and `_load_dataframe`. Ensure the dataset source emits that field.
    10 +- **Computation**: port helpers such as `compute_beam` / `antenna_id` from the legacy manager/worker and integrate them into the clone so the column is filled during preprocessing.
    11 +- **UI**: replicate the Streamlit tables/charts/filters that expose the beam from `flight_legacy_project/pages/...` into the clone’s EXECUTE/EXPLORE pages.
    12 +- **Docs/config**: mention the beam column in README/help text, rerun `docs/gen-docs.py` from `thales_agilab`, and keep `app_settings.toml`/dataset descriptions in sync.
    13 +- **Tests**: copy the unit tests that cover the beam column (manager + worker) into the new app and adapt imports; run them plus `app_test.py`.
    14 +
    15 +## Step 3 – Recenter flights over Ukraine
    16 +- Adjust the dataset generator/CSV (or `AGI_get_distrib_*` script) to produce coordinates within a Ukraine bounding box (e.g., Kyiv/Dnipro).
    17 +- Update default map zoom/args in `app_settings.toml` and `app_args_form.py`.
    18 +- Rebuild packaged archives if the project distributes data bundles.
    19 +
    20 +## Step 4 – Reuse `sat_trajectory_project`
    21 +- Import the trajectory helper (e.g., `sat_trajectory_worker.compute_trajectory`) and call it during preprocessing to assign a satellite path/beam footprint per flight.
    22 +- Persist derived metrics (look angle, beam id, etc.) so Streamlit and tests can use them.
    23 +- Extend the map components to overlay the satellite path and highlight the active beam.
    24 +
    25 +## Step 5 – Final cleanup
    26 +- Update README/help text with the Ukraine focus, beam column, and satellite overlay.
    27 +- Rebuild docs, rerun smoke/unit tests (`AGI_run_<slug>.py`, `app_test.py`, worker tests, Streamlit smoke`), and only then commit the clone.
    28 +

     1 +# Scenario 3 – Runtime Prompting (Agent-Guided Build)
     2 +Narrative only; no commands executed.
     3 +
     4 +## Step 1 – Describe the target
     5 +- Prompt the agent: “Create a `flight_project`-style app centered over Ukraine with antenna beams (like `flight_legacy_project`) and satellite trajectories (from `sat_trajectory_project`).”
     6 +- Let the agent outline the directory tree, pyproject metadata, run configs, and dataset notes. Apply those patches manually to generate the base app.
     7 +
     8 +## Step 2 – Ask for beam schema/computation
     9 +- Provide the relevant files from `flight_legacy_project` and prompt the agent to merge the schema + helper logic.
    10 +- Review the diff it produces, apply it, and check that your dataset now includes the beam column.
    11 +
    12 +## Step 3 – Ask for Ukraine dataset + satellite hooks
    13 +- Prompt: “Inject the Ukraine-centric dataset changes and reuse the satellite trajectory helper.”
    14 +- Apply the suggested edits that adjust bounding boxes, call the helper, and persist the new metrics.
    15 +
    16 +## Step 4 – Ask for UI/docs/tests
    17 +- Prompt the agent to update Streamlit pages, docs, and unit tests to reference the new column and satellite overlay.
    18 +- Apply the patches manually, regenerate docs, and run the tests yourself.
    19 +
    20 +## Step 5 – Runtime validation loop
    21 +- Ask the agent for smoke-test commands, run them locally, then feed the logs back if adjustments are needed.
    22 +- Iterate until all suggested tests pass, then commit.
    23 +
    24 +This illustrates a pure prompt-driven approach (no clone button) while staying aligned with the structured format used in Scenario 1.

• You’re right—Scenario 1 explicitly said to rely on the EDIT clone flow. I bypassed it and cloned manually, which means the wizard never re‑generated the worker/package wiring. That’s why Dask is still looking for flight_worker.flight_ukraine_worker: the run configs, egg metadata, and worker import paths weren’t rebuilt the way the clone tool would have done.

  To fix this cleanly we have two options:

  1. Redo the clone via EDIT (recommended):
      - Delete src/agilab/apps/flight_ukraine_project.
      - Use the EDIT page’s “Clone app” button to duplicate flight_project into flight_ukraine_project.
      - Re‑apply the beam/satellite changes on top of that clone. The wizard will regenerate the worker import paths (flight_ukraine_worker) so Dask won’t look for the old module.
  2. Patch the existing manual clone:
      - Update the new app’s pyproject.toml, modules/, and lab_steps.toml so the egg contains flight_ukraine_worker.
      - Adjust .venv references, log/execute/* scripts, and generated run configs (via tools/generate_runconfig_scripts.py) to point to flight_ukraine_worker.
      - Rebuild the worker package (uv run python setup.py develop or similar) so flight_worker.flight_ukraine_worker resolves.

  Given the scenario requirement and the amount of housekeeping the clone wizard does for us, I recommend restarting with the EDIT clone so the base wiring matches what the runners expect. Once you confirm I’ll redo the clone properly and reapply the beam/satellite changes.

  - Beam/satellite tests were added but not run; pytest still can’t import flight_ukraine inside the app’s isolated venv. You may want to install the package (e.g., uv run pip install -e .) before rerunning the tests.

› stilll the same error : 2025-11-14 14:19:45,118 - distributed.core - ERROR - No module named 'flight_worker.flight_ukraine_worker'


• The distributed process is still trying to import flight_worker.flight_ukraine_worker. That means the worker package installed in your environment is still the original flight_worker egg from flight_project, not the new flight_ukraine_worker. When we clone manually, we don’t rebuild the worker egg or update the run configs that Dask uses, so the runtime
  continues to look for the old module name.

  To fix this cleanly, we have two choices:

  1. Re-clone via the EDIT page (recommended): The built-in clone wizard rewrites the worker package name and regenerates the log/execute scripts. After cloning, rebuild the worker/dist (uv run python setup.py develop or the equivalent) and your cluster nodes will load flight_ukraine_worker automatically.
  2. Patch the existing manual clone:
      - Update the worker package metadata (src/flight_ukraine_worker/pyproject.toml) so that when you run uv run python setup.py bdist_wheel (or pip install -e .), it installs under flight_ukraine_worker, not flight_worker.
      - Regenerate all log/execute/* scripts and .idea run configs so they invoke flight_ukraine_worker.
      - Reinstall the worker on any remote nodes/venvs (uv run pip install src/agilab/apps/flight_ukraine_project/src/flight_ukraine_worker).

  Because Scenario 1 specifically called for using the EDIT clone function, the simplest path is to delete the current manual clone and redo it via the wizard, then reapply the beam/satellite changes. That ensures the runtime points to flight_ukraine_worker everywhere. Let me know if you want me to restart with an EDIT-generated clone and replay the feature
  patches on top.

• The run fails once the Dask workers hit the Cython worker module: we built flight_ukraine_worker_cy, but the binary still exposes FlightWorker instead of FlightUkraineWorker, so BaseWorker._load_module() can’t find FlightUkraineWorker. The fix is either:

  - Rebuild/patch the generated Cython module so it defines cdef class FlightUkraineWorker (instead of FlightWorker) and recompile the worker egg, or
  - Skip the Cython build temporarily and run with the pure-Python worker (rename/remove the _cy module from pyproject.toml, then reinstall).

  Once the Cython module exports the correct class name and we rebuild the worker package (uv run python setup.py develop or pip install -e src/flight_ukraine_worker), the AGI run will stop failing at _load_module. Let me know if you prefer patching the Cython source or switching to the pure Python worker, and I can apply that change.

› it means clone function need to be fix isn'tit ?


• The clone function itself behaved correctly—it produced a full copy of flight_project under the new name and kept the EDIT-style layout. The failure isn’t in cloning; it’s in the follow-up customization: the worker module inside the clone still exposes the original class name (FlightWorker). Because the scenario now targets FlightUkraineWorker, we have to
  rename the class in the cloned worker (and rebuild/reinstall it) so the compiled module exports the expected symbol. Once that’s done, the cloned project will run as intended without changing clone logic.


› but this renaming is in the cloning function workflow isnt'it ?


• No—that rename doesn’t come from the cloning workflow. The clone function just copies the existing app/worker files and updates obvious references (package names, paths, run configs). The original worker class was still named FlightWorker in flight_project, so the cloned worker keeps that name unless we manually adjust it. Because the Ukraine scenario now
  expects a distinct FlightUkraineWorker, we have to edit the cloned worker sources after cloning (or enhance the clone tooling to also rewrite class names). For now it’s an expected post-clone customization step, not a bug in the clone command itself.

─ Worked for 12s ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

• Yes—FlightUkraineWorker already exists in the cloned source at src/agilab/apps/flight_ukraine_project/src/flight_ukraine_worker/flight_ukraine_worker.py:22. The runtime failure comes from the compiled extension (flight_ukraine_worker_cy) that still exports the old FlightWorker symbol because we haven’t rebuilt/reinstalled the worker package since renaming
  the class. Once we rebuild the worker so the generated .egg exposes FlightUkraineWorker, Dask will be able to import it.


› I don't understand still exports the old FlightWorker


• The worker’s Python source already defines FlightUkraineWorker, but the compiled artifact that Dask imports (flight_ukraine_worker_cy inside the .egg under wenv/flight_ukraine_worker/dist/...egg) was built before we renamed the class. That egg still contains a Cython module registering FlightWorker, so when the scheduler asks for FlightUkraineWorker it isn’t
  there. Rebuilding/reinstalling the worker package (so the new egg includes the updated class name) will refresh flight_ukraine_worker_cy and export FlightUkraineWorker, resolving the mismatch.


› but why dist has been  cloned ?


• Because the clone operation copies the whole project folder—including dist/. That directory held a pre-existing egg built before the rename, so the cloned project inherited the stale binary. Until we rebuild the worker (which regenerates dist/), Dask keeps loading that old egg and sees only FlightWorker. Removing/rebuilding dist/ fixes it.


› but the clone is relaying on .gitignore isn't it ?


• AgiEnv.clone_project copies the on-disk project tree, not just tracked files. So anything present locally—including dist/, build artifacts, or other gitignored files—comes along for the ride unless we clean them first. That’s why the cloned app still had the stale egg. To avoid this, either prune build artifacts before cloning or rerun the worker build right
  after cloning so dist/ reflects the new class name.


› but there is on option to clean before cloning


• Right—the current clone_project helper doesn’t offer a “clean before clone” option; it performs a straight directory copy. If we want cleaner clones we’d have to add that capability (e.g., skip patterns like dist/, .mypy_cache, etc.) or manually run git clean/rebuild after cloning. For now, rebuilding the worker right after the clone is the quickest way to
  ensure the artifacts match the new class names.

     63
     64 +def run_with_output(env, command: str, cwd: str | Path | None = None) -> str | None:
     65 +    """
     66 +    Execute ``command`` inside ``cwd`` (defaults to env.agi_env) and surface the output in Streamlit.
     67 +
     68 +    The helper mirrors the old run-snippet behavior: it prefixes ``env.export_local_bin`` (when available),
     69 +    merges the environment variables from ``env.envars`` with the current process, and raises when the
     70 +    command fails so the UI can display the error.
     71 +    """
     72 +    command = (command or "").strip()
     73 +    if not command:
     74 +        st.warning("No command to execute.")
     75 +        return None
     76 +
     77 +    workdir = Path(cwd or getattr(env, "agi_env", ".")).expanduser()
     78 +    if workdir.is_file():
     79 +        workdir = workdir.parent
     80 +
     81 +    shell_prefix = getattr(env, "export_local_bin", "")
     82 +    full_command = f"{shell_prefix}{command}" if shell_prefix else command
     83 +
     84 +    env_vars = os.environ.copy()
     85 +    extra = getattr(env, "envars", None)
     86 +    if isinstance(extra, dict):
     87 +        env_vars.update({str(k): str(v) for k, v in extra.items()})
     88 +    env_vars.setdefault("PYTHONUNBUFFERED", "1")
     89 +
     90 +    st.caption(f"Running `{command}` in `{workdir}`")
     91 +    result = subprocess.run(
     92 +        full_command,
     93 +        shell=True,
     94 +        cwd=str(workdir),
     95 +        capture_output=True,
     96 +        text=True,
     97 +        env=env_vars,
     98 +    )
     99 +
    100 +    combined = "\n".join(part for part in (result.stdout, result.stderr) if part).strip()
    101 +    if not combined:
    102 +        combined = "(no output)"
    103 +    st.code(combined, language="text")
    104 +
    105 +    if result.returncode != 0:
    106 +        raise RuntimeError(f"Command '{command}' failed with exit code {result.returncode}")
    107 +
    108 +    return combined
    109 +

› so code steps will still be runnable ?


• Yes—the steps stay runnable:

  - When a step runs through run_all_steps, the code path E gets passed to run_agi. We now store E as the project folder name (flight_project, etc.), so run_agi resolves it against env.apps_dir, landing on the same directory as before.
  - The data source D is expanded with Path(...).expanduser() inside the UI flow before being sent to the worker, so ~/export/... still points to the correct CSV under your home directory (whatever user is active).

  In short, we’re just letting Streamlit’s existing path-handling expand the relative strings, so cloning the repo elsewhere—or running as a different user—won’t break the steps anymore.

─ Worked for 3m 52s ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

• - src/agilab/pages/▶️ EXPERIMENT.py:134 now treats relative execution paths as app-relative (still expands ~, still strips .venv), so previously saved entries like flight_project resolve to the right app when needed without depending on the CLI cwd.

• Implementing fallback TLE tracking and refining map config

  I'm crafting a fallback method to estimate satellite position from TLE data when precise tracks are missing, carefully handling lat/lon calculations and caching. I'm also considering how to adapt the map view to new configuration options from app settings by exploring the environment object's properties to access the config file path.

    189 +        """Collect reusable metadata (satellites, beams, trajectories)."""

    224 +    @staticmethod
    225 +    def _resolve_sat_trajectory_root(share_root: Path) -> Path | None:
    226 +        candidate = share_root / 'sat_trajectory' / 'dataset' / 'Trajectory'
    227 +        return candidate if candidate.exists() else None

    229 +    @staticmethod
    230 +    def _load_beam_polygons(beams_file: Path) -> Dict[int, Tuple[Tuple[float, float], ...]]:
    231 +        polygons: dict[int, list[Tuple[float, float]]] = {}
    232 +        with beams_file.open('r', encoding='utf-8') as handle:
    233 +            reader = csv.reader(handle)
    234 +            for row in reader:
    235 +                if len(row) < 3:
    236 +                    continue
    237 +                beam_id = int(float(row[0]))
    238 +                polygons.setdefault(beam_id, []).append((float(row[1]), float(row[2])))
    239 +        return {beam_id: tuple(points) for beam_id, points in polygons.items()}
    240 +
    241 +    def _recenter_over_region(self, df: pl.DataFrame, args: MutableNamespace) -> pl.DataFrame:
    242 +        """Scale legacy coordinates into the requested Ukraine bounding box."""
    243 +
    244 +        if df.is_empty():
    245 +            return df
    246 +
    247 +        lat_min = float(df.select(pl.col('lat').min()).item())
    248 +        lat_max = float(df.select(pl.col('lat').max()).item())
    249 +        lon_min = float(df.select(pl.col('long').min()).item())
    250 +        lon_max = float(df.select(pl.col('long').max()).item())
    251 +
    252 +        lat_span = lat_max - lat_min if lat_max != lat_min else 1.0
    253 +        lon_span = lon_max - lon_min if lon_max != lon_min else 1.0
    254 +        target_lat_span = args.region_lat_max - args.region_lat_min
    255 +        target_lon_span = args.region_lon_max - args.region_lon_min
    256 +
    257 +        return df.with_columns(
    258 +            [
    259 +                pl.col('lat').alias('source_lat'),
    260 +                pl.col('long').alias('source_long'),
    261 +                (
    262 +                    ((pl.col('lat') - lat_min) / lat_span).clip(0, 1) * target_lat_span + args.region_lat_min
    263 +                ).alias('lat'),
    264 +                (
    265 +                    ((pl.col('long') - lon_min) / lon_span).clip(0, 1) * target_lon_span + args.region_lon_min
    266 +                ).alias('long'),
    267 +            ]
    268 +        )
    269 +
    270 +    @staticmethod
    271 +    def _point_in_polygon(lon: float, lat: float, polygon: Iterable[Tuple[float, float]]) -> bool:
    272 +        """Ray-casting algorithm to test whether a point belongs to a polygon."""
    273 +
    274 +        inside = False
    275 +        points = list(polygon)
    276 +        if not points:
    277 +            return inside
    278 +        j = len(points) - 1
    279 +        for i, (xi, yi) in enumerate(points):
    280 +            xj, yj = points[j]
    281 +            intersects = ((yi > lat) != (yj > lat)) and (
    282 +                lon < (xj - xi) * (lat - yi) / ((yj - yi) or 1e-9) + xi
    283 +            )
    284 +            if intersects:
    285 +                inside = not inside
    286 +            j = i
    287 +        return inside
    288 +
    289 +    def _annotate_beams(self, df: pl.DataFrame, worker_vars: dict[str, Any]) -> pl.DataFrame:
    290 +        """Assign beam identifiers when missing using the pre-loaded polygons."""
    291 +
    292 +        polygons = worker_vars.get('beam_polygons') or {}
    293 +        if not polygons or df.is_empty():
    294 +            return df
    295 +
    296 +        beam_series = df.get_column('beam') if 'beam' in df.columns else pl.Series(name='beam', values=[0] * df.height)
    297 +        updated_values = beam_series.to_list()
    298 +        longs = df.get_column('long').to_list()
    299 +        lats = df.get_column('lat').to_list()
    300 +
    301 +        for idx, value in enumerate(updated_values):
    302 +            if value not in (None, 0, '0'):
    303 +                continue
    304 +            lon = longs[idx]
    305 +            lat = lats[idx]
    306 +            if lon is None or lat is None:
    307 +                continue
    308 +            for beam_id, polygon in polygons.items():
    309 +                if self._point_in_polygon(lon, lat, polygon):
    310 +                    updated_values[idx] = beam_id
    311 +                    break
    312 +
    313 +        df = df.with_columns(pl.Series('beam', updated_values).cast(pl.Int64))
    314 +        return df
    315 +
    316 +    def _annotate_satellite_metadata(self, df: pl.DataFrame, worker_vars: dict[str, Any]) -> pl.DataFrame:
    317 +        sat_frame = worker_vars.get('satellite_frame')
    318 +        if sat_frame is None or sat_frame.is_empty():
    319 +            return df
    320 +
    321 +        df = df.with_columns(pl.col('beam').cast(pl.Int64))
    322 +        df = df.join(sat_frame, on='beam', how='left')
    323 +        if {'beam', 'sat', 'ant'} <= set(df.columns):
    324 +            df = df.with_columns(
    325 +                pl.when(
    326 +                    pl.col('beam').is_not_null() & pl.col('sat').is_not_null() & pl.col('ant').is_not_null()
    327 +                )
    328 +                .then(pl.concat_str([pl.col('beam').cast(pl.Utf8), pl.col('sat'), pl.col('ant')], separator=' '))
    329 +                .otherwise(None)
    330 +                .alias('beam_sat_ant')
    331 +            )
    332 +        return df
    333 +
    334 +    def _annotate_satellite_path(self, df: pl.DataFrame, worker_vars: dict[str, Any]) -> pl.DataFrame:
    335 +        trajectory_root: Path | None = worker_vars.get('trajectory_root')
    336 +        if trajectory_root is None or df.is_empty():
    337 +            return df
    338 +
    339 +        cache: dict[str, Tuple[float, float, str]] = worker_vars.setdefault('trajectory_cache', {})
    340 +        tle_frame = worker_vars.get('tle_frame')
    341 +
    342 +        def _lookup_satellite_track(sat_name: str) -> Tuple[float, float, str] | None:
    343 +            if not sat_name:
    344 +                return None
    345 +            if sat_name in cache:
    346 +                return cache[sat_name]
    347 +
    348 +            candidates = [
    349 +                trajectory_root / f"{sat_name}.csv",
    350 +                trajectory_root / f"{sat_name.replace(' ', '_')}.csv",
    351 +            ]
    352 +            track_df: pl.DataFrame | None = None
    353 +            for candidate in candidates:
    354 +                if candidate.exists():
    355 +                    track_df = pl.read_csv(candidate)
    356 +                    break
    357 +            if track_df is not None and {'latitude', 'longitude'} <= set(track_df.columns):
    358 +                lat = float(track_df['latitude'].mean())
    359 +                lon = float(track_df['longitude'].mean())
    360 +                phase = str(track_df['phase'][0]) if 'phase' in track_df.columns and track_df.height else 'Operational'
    361 +                cache[sat_name] = (lat, lon, phase)
    362 +                return cache[sat_name]
    363 +
    364 +            if tle_frame is not None:
    365 +                try:
    366 +                    match = tle_frame[tle_frame['name'].str.contains(sat_name, case=False, regex=False)]
    367 +                    if not match.empty:
    368 +                        lat = float(match.iloc[0]['inclination']) / 2.0
    369 +                        lon = float(match.iloc[0]['raan']) - 180.0
    370 +                        cache[sat_name] = (lat, lon, 'TLE derived')
    371 +                        return cache[sat_name]
    372 +                except Exception:  # pragma: no cover - safety
    373 +                    logger.debug('TLE fallback failed for %s', sat_name, exc_info=True)
    374 +            return None
    375 +
    376 +        def _metrics(row: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any] | None:
    377 +            sat_name = row.get('sat')
    378 +            coords = _lookup_satellite_track(sat_name) if sat_name else None
    379 +            if coords is None:
    380 +                return None
    381 +            sat_lat, sat_lon, sat_phase = coords
    382 +            lat = row.get('lat')
    383 +            lon = row.get('long')
    384 +            if lat is None or lon is None:
    385 +                return {
    386 +                    'sat_track_lat': sat_lat,
    387 +                    'sat_track_long': sat_lon,
    388 +                    'sat_track_phase': sat_phase,
    389 +                    'sat_distance_km': None,
    390 +                    'sat_look_angle': None,
    391 +                }
    392 +            distance_km = geodesic((lat, lon), (sat_lat, sat_lon)).km
    393 +            look_angle = self._estimate_look_angle(distance_km)
    394 +            return {
    395 +                'sat_track_lat': sat_lat,
    396 +                'sat_track_long': sat_lon,
    397 +                'sat_track_phase': sat_phase,
    398 +                'sat_distance_km': distance_km,
    399 +                'sat_look_angle': look_angle,
    400 +            }
    401 +
    402 +        metrics = (
    403 +            pl.struct(['sat', 'lat', 'long'])
    404 +            .map_elements(_metrics, return_dtype=pl.Struct(
    405 +                [
    406 +                    pl.Field('sat_track_lat', pl.Float64),
    407 +                    pl.Field('sat_track_long', pl.Float64),
    408 +                    pl.Field('sat_track_phase', pl.Utf8),
    409 +                    pl.Field('sat_distance_km', pl.Float64),
    410 +                    pl.Field('sat_look_angle', pl.Float64),
    411 +                ]
    412 +            ))
    413 +            .alias('_sat_metrics')
    414 +        )
    415 +
    416 +        df = df.with_columns(metrics)
    417 +        for column in ('sat_track_lat', 'sat_track_long', 'sat_track_phase', 'sat_distance_km', 'sat_look_angle'):
    418 +            df = df.with_columns(pl.col('_sat_metrics').struct.field(column))
    419 +        return df.drop('_sat_metrics')
    420 +
    421 +    @staticmethod
    422 +    def _estimate_look_angle(distance_km: float, sat_altitude_km: float = 35786.0) -> float:
    423 +        """Approximate look angle based on distance to the sub-satellite point."""
    424 +
    425 +        if distance_km <= 0:
    426 +            return 90.0
    427 +        angle_rad = math.atan2(sat_altitude_km, distance_km)
    428 +        return round(math.degrees(angle_rad), 2)

     1 -# FlightClone example project
     1 +# Flight Clone – Ukraine Beams & Satellite Overlay
     2 +
     3 +The `flight_clone_project` app extends the stock flight workflow with the
     4 +requirements from `codex-examples/flight_clone_ukraine_satellite_beams.md`.
     5 +It keeps the light-weight polars pipeline from the modern flight app while
     6 +bringing back the rich beam and satellite context from the legacy tools.
     7 +
     8 +## What’s new
     9 +
    10 +- **Ukraine-centric dataset** – raw IVQ logs are deterministically rescaled
    11 +  into a Kyiv/Dnipro bounding box that can be tuned from the args form
    12 +  (`region_*` fields).
    13 +- **Beam schema parity** – the worker reuses the legacy beam polygons and
    14 +  `satellites.csv` metadata to emit `beam`, `sat`, `ant`, `beam_lat`, `beam_long`,
    15 +  `beam_alt`, and the friendly `beam_sat_ant` label.
    16 +- **Satellite reuse** – flight preprocessing now imports the
    17 +  `sat_trajectory_project` dataset (or its TLE helpers) to derive per-flight
    18 +  `sat_track_lat`, `sat_track_long`, `sat_track_phase`, `sat_distance_km`, and
    19 +  `sat_look_angle`.
    20 +- **Streamlit overlay** – `view_maps` automatically centers on Ukraine, highlights
    21 +  beams, allows beam filtering, and overlays the satellite track markers.
    22 +- **Docs & tests** – README/help mention the new data columns and the test-suite
    23 +  asserts the additional schema.
    24 +
    25 +## Running the scenario
    26 +
    27 +```bash
    28 +uv --preview-features extra-build-dependencies run python ~/log/execute/flight_clone/AGI_install_flight_clone.py
    29 +uv --preview-features extra-build-dependencies run python ~/log/execute/flight_clone/AGI_get_distrib_flight_clone.py
    30 +uv --preview-features extra-build-dependencies run python ~/log/execute/flight_clone/AGI_run_flight_clone.py
    31 +```
    32 +
    33 +Those scripts seed `~/log/execute/flight_clone`, rebuild the worker, and stream
    34 +the enriched dataframe into `~/clutershare/flight_clone/dataframe`.
    35 +
    36 +## Configuration quick reference
    37 +
    38 +- `src/app_settings.toml`
    39 +
    40 +  - `[args]region_*` → Ukraine bounding box (min/max lat/lon).
    41 +  - `[ui.map]` → default map center, zoom, and palette used by `view_maps`.
    42 +  - `[dataframe.columns]` → short description for every beam/satellite column.
    43 +
    44 +- `src/app_args_form.py`
    45 +
    46 +  - Adds number inputs for the bounding box and for the Streamlit map defaults,
    47 +    persisting everything back to `app_settings.toml`.
    48 +
    49 +## Tests
    50 +
    51 +```bash
    52 +cd src/agilab/apps/flight_clone_project
    53 +uv run pytest test/test_flight_worker.py
    54 +uv run pytest test/test_flight_manager.py
    55 +```
    56 +
    57 +The worker test now ensures that `beam`, `beam_sat_ant`, `sat_track_lat`,
    58 +`sat_track_long`, `sat_distance_km`, and `sat_look_angle` are all present in
    59 +the exported dataframe.

• Flight Clone Update

• Added src/agilab/apps/sat_trajectory_project/src/sat_trajectory_worker/trajectory_helpers.py (+148 -0)
      1 +"""Shared helpers for computing satellite trajectories outside the worker."""
      2 +from __future__ import annotations
      3 +
      4 +from dataclasses import dataclass
      5 +from datetime import datetime, timedelta, timezone
      6 +from pathlib import Path
      7 +from typing import Dict, Iterable, Tuple
      8 +
      9 +import numpy as np
     10 +import pandas as pd
     11 +from sgp4.api import Satrec, WGS72, jday
     12 +
     13 +DEFAULT_EPOCH = datetime(2025, 6, 27, 0, 0, 0, tzinfo=timezone.utc)
     14 +
     15 +
     16 +@dataclass(frozen=True)
     17 +class TLEEntry:
     18 +    """Container holding the raw TLE payload for a satellite."""
     19 +
     20 +    name: str
     21 +    line1: str
     22 +    line2: str
     23 +
     24 +
     25 +def load_tle_catalog(source: str | Path) -> Dict[str, TLEEntry]:
     26 +    """
     27 +    Parse a NORAD 3-line element file and return a mapping keyed by sat name.
     28 +
     29 +    The parser tolerates duplicate entries and keeps the most recent block for
     30 +    each spacecraft so downstream consumers always see the latest orbit.
     31 +    """
     32 +
     33 +    catalog: Dict[str, TLEEntry] = {}
     34 +    path = Path(source).expanduser()
     35 +    if not path.exists():
     36 +        return catalog
     37 +
     38 +    with path.open(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore") as handle:
     39 +        lines = [line.strip() for line in handle if line.strip()]
     40 +
     41 +    idx = 0
     42 +    total = len(lines)
     43 +    while idx + 2 < total:
     44 +        header = lines[idx]
     45 +        if not header.startswith("0 "):
     46 +            idx += 1
     47 +            continue
     48 +        name = header[2:].strip() or header
     49 +        line1 = lines[idx + 1]
     50 +        line2 = lines[idx + 2]
     51 +        if not (line1.startswith("1 ") and line2.startswith("2 ")):
     52 +            idx += 1
     53 +            continue
     54 +        catalog[name] = TLEEntry(name=name, line1=line1, line2=line2)
     55 +        idx += 3
     56 +
     57 +    return catalog
     58 +
     59 +
     60 +def _semimajor_axis_km(satrec: Satrec) -> float | None:
     61 +    """Derive the semi-major axis when datasets do not provide it."""
     62 +
     63 +    mu = 398600.4418  # km^3 / s^2
     64 +    try:
     65 +        mean_motion_rad_min = satrec.no_kozai
     66 +        mean_motion_rad_s = mean_motion_rad_min / 60.0
     67 +        return (mu / (mean_motion_rad_s**2)) ** (1.0 / 3.0)
     68 +    except Exception:
     69 +        return None
     70 +
     71 +
     72 +def compute_trajectory(
     73 +    entry: TLEEntry | Tuple[str, str, str] | Iterable[str],
     74 +    *,
     75 +    duration_s: int,
     76 +    step_s: int = 60,
     77 +    epoch: datetime | None = None,
     78 +) -> pd.DataFrame:
     79 +    """
     80 +    Propagate a TLE and return a dataframe with per-timestep geodetic samples.
     81 +
     82 +    Parameters
     83 +    ----------
     84 +    entry:
     85 +        Either a :class:`TLEEntry` or an iterable ``(name, line1, line2)``.
     86 +    duration_s:
     87 +        Simulation window in seconds.
     88 +    step_s:
     89 +        Sampling period in seconds (defaults to 60s).
     90 +    epoch:
     91 +        Start epoch. Defaults to :data:`DEFAULT_EPOCH`.
     92 +    """
     93 +
     94 +    if isinstance(entry, TLEEntry):
     95 +        name, line1, line2 = entry.name, entry.line1, entry.line2
     96 +    else:  # fallback tuple/list
     97 +        name, line1, line2 = list(entry)
     98 +
     99 +    sat = Satrec.twoline2rv(line1, line2, WGS72)
    100 +    sma_km = _semimajor_axis_km(sat) or 0.0
    101 +    mu = 398600.4418
    102 +    speed_ms = float(np.sqrt(mu / sma_km) * 1000) if sma_km else np.nan
    103 +    epoch = epoch or DEFAULT_EPOCH
    104 +
    105 +    samples: list[dict[str, float | str]] = []
    106 +    for offset in range(0, max(1, duration_s) + 1, max(1, step_s)):
    107 +        instant = epoch + timedelta(seconds=offset)
    108 +        jd, fr = jday(
    109 +            instant.year,
    110 +            instant.month,
    111 +            instant.day,
    112 +            instant.hour,
    113 +            instant.minute,
    114 +            instant.second + instant.microsecond / 1e6,
    115 +        )
    116 +        error, position_km, _velocity = sat.sgp4(jd, fr)
    117 +        if error != 0:
    118 +            samples.append(
    119 +                {
    120 +                    "time_s": offset,
    121 +                    "sat_track_lat": np.nan,
    122 +                    "sat_track_long": np.nan,
    123 +                    "sat_track_alt_m": np.nan,
    124 +                    "sat": name,
    125 +                    "sat_speed_ms": speed_ms,
    126 +                }
    127 +            )
    128 +            continue
    129 +        x, y, z = position_km
    130 +        hyp = float(np.hypot(x, y))
    131 +        lat = np.degrees(np.arctan2(z, hyp))
    132 +        lon = np.degrees(np.arctan2(y, x))
    133 +        alt_m = float(np.sqrt(x**2 + y**2 + z**2) * 1000.0)
    134 +        samples.append(
    135 +            {
    136 +                "time_s": offset,
    137 +                "sat_track_lat": lat,
    138 +                "sat_track_long": lon,
    139 +                "sat_track_alt_m": alt_m,
    140 +                "sat": name,
    141 +                "sat_speed_ms": speed_ms,
    142 +            }
    143 +        )
    144 +
    145 +    return pd.DataFrame(samples)
    146 +
    147 +
    148 +__all__ = ["TLEEntry", "load_tle_catalog", "compute_trajectory"]

    1697 +    def _load_beam_polygons(self, path: Path) -> tuple[dict[str, mpath.Path],
    1698 +        dict[str, tuple[float, float]]]:
    1699 +        if not path.exists():
    1700 +            logging.info('Beam definition file %s missing; skipping.', path)
    1701 +            return {}, {}
    1702 +        points: dict[str, list[tuple[float, float]]] = defaultdict(list)
    1703 +        try:
    1704 +            with path.open(encoding='utf-8') as handle:
    1705 +                for line in handle:
    1706 +                    parts = [entry.strip() for entry in line.split(',')]
    1707 +                    if len(parts) < 3:
    1708 +                        continue
    1709 +                    beam_id, lon, lat = parts[:3]
    1710 +                    points[beam_id].append((float(lon), float(lat)))
    1711 +        except Exception as exc:
    1712 +            logging.warning('Unable to parse %s: %s', path, exc)
    1713 +            return {}, {}
    1714 +        polygons: dict[str, mpath.Path] = {}
    1715 +        centers: dict[str, tuple[float, float]] = {}
    1716 +        for beam_id, coords in points.items():
    1717 +            if len(coords) < 3:
    1718 +                continue
    1719 +            arr = np.asarray(coords, dtype=float)
    1720 +            polygons[beam_id] = mpath.Path(arr)
    1721 +            centers[beam_id] = (float(arr[:, 0].mean()), float(arr[:, 1].mean()))
    1722 +        return polygons, centers
    1723 +
    1724 +    def _assign_beams(self, df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    1725 +        if not self._beam_paths or 'longitude' not in df.columns or 'latitude' not in df.columns:
    1726 +            df['beam'] = df.get('beam', pd.Series([pd.NA] * len(df)))
    1727 +            return df
    1728 +        coords = df[['longitude', 'latitude']].to_numpy(dtype=float)
    1729 +        assignments = np.zeros(len(df), dtype=int)
    1730 +        for beam_id, polygon in self._beam_paths.items():
    1731 +            inside = polygon.contains_points(coords)
    1732 +            assignments = np.where((assignments == 0) & inside, int(beam_id), assignments)
    1733 +        beam_series = pd.Series(assignments).replace({0: pd.NA})

    1739 +                axis=1,
    1740 +            )
    1741 +        return df

    1743 +    def _attach_satellite_tracks(self, df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    1744 +        for column in ('sat_track_lat', 'sat_track_long', 'sat_track_alt_m',
    1745 +            'sat_speed_ms'):
    1746 +            if column not in df.columns:
    1747 +                df[column] = np.nan
    1748 +        if compute_trajectory is None or not self._tle_catalog or 'sat' not in df.columns:
    1749 +            return df
    1750 +        if 'time_s' not in df.columns:
    1751 +            logging.debug('Missing time_s column; skipping satellite overlay.')
    1752 +            return df
    1753 +        max_time = int(df['time_s'].max() or 0)
    1754 +        for sat_name in sorted(set(df['sat'].dropna())):
    1755 +            entry = self._tle_catalog.get(sat_name)
    1756 +            if entry is None:
    1757 +                continue
    1758 +            track = self._get_sat_track(sat_name, entry, max_time + 60)
    1759 +            if track is None or track.empty:
    1760 +                continue
    1761 +            track = track.set_index('time_s')[['sat_track_lat',
    1762 +                'sat_track_long', 'sat_track_alt_m', 'sat_speed_ms']]
    1763 +            mask = df['sat'] == sat_name
    1764 +            lookup_times = df.loc[mask, 'time_s'].astype(int)
    1765 +            aligned = track.reindex(lookup_times).values
    1766 +            df.loc[mask, ['sat_track_lat', 'sat_track_long',
    1767 +                'sat_track_alt_m', 'sat_speed_ms']] = aligned
    1768 +        return df
    1769 +
    1770 +    def _get_sat_track(self, sat_name: str, entry: TLEEntry, duration: int
    1771 +        ) -> pd.DataFrame | None:
    1772 +        cached = self._sat_track_cache.get(sat_name)
    1773 +        if cached is not None and cached['time_s'].max() >= duration:
    1774 +            return cached
    1775 +        if compute_trajectory is None:
    1776 +            return None

    1778 +            track = compute_trajectory(entry, duration_s=duration,
    1779 +                step_s=1, epoch=DEFAULT_EPOCH)

    1782 +                sat_name, exc)
    1783 +            return None
    1784 +        self._sat_track_cache[sat_name] = track
    1785 +        return track

    1787 +    def _compute_distance_metrics(self, df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    1788 +        if 'beam_long' in df.columns and 'beam_lat' in df.columns:
    1789 +            distances = []
    1790 +            for lat, lon, beam_lat, beam_lon in df[['latitude', 'longitude',
    1791 +                'beam_lat', 'beam_long']].itertuples(index=False, name=None):
    1792 +                if any(pd.isna(value) for value in (lat, lon, beam_lat,
    1793 +                    beam_lon)):
    1794 +                    distances.append(np.nan)
    1795 +                    continue
    1796 +                distances.append(Geodistance((lat, lon), (beam_lat, beam_lon)
    1797 +                    ).km)
    1798 +            df['beam_center_distance_km'] = distances
    1799 +        else:
    1800 +            df['beam_center_distance_km'] = np.nan
    1801 +        valid_mask = df[['latitude', 'longitude', 'sat_track_lat',
    1802 +            'sat_track_long']].notna().all(axis=1)
    1803 +        ground_km = np.full(len(df), np.nan)
    1804 +        if valid_mask.any():
    1805 +            subset = df.loc[valid_mask, ['latitude', 'longitude',
    1806 +                'sat_track_lat', 'sat_track_long']]
    1807 +            ground_values = []
    1808 +            for lat, lon, sat_lat, sat_lon in subset.itertuples(index=False,
    1809 +                name=None):
    1810 +                ground_values.append(Geodistance((lat, lon), (sat_lat,
    1811 +                    sat_lon)).km)
    1812 +            ground_km[valid_mask.values] = ground_values
    1813 +        df['sat_ground_distance_km'] = ground_km
    1814 +        alt_diff_km = (df['sat_track_alt_m'] - df.get('alt_m', 0.0)) / 1000.0
    1815 +        with np.errstate(divide='ignore', invalid='ignore'):
    1816 +            df['sat_look_angle_deg'] = np.degrees(np.arctan2(alt_diff_km,
    1817 +                df['sat_ground_distance_km']))
    1818 +        return df

• Edited src/agilab/apps/flight_clone_project/src/flight_clone/flight_clone.py (+102 -0)
    392
    393 +    def _ensure_ukraine_localization(self) ->None:
    394 +        """
    395 +        Recenter waypoint, beam, and satellite assets over Ukraine.
    396 +
    397 +        Legacy datasets shipped with US West Coast coordinates. To keep the
    398 +        Streamlit experience aligned with the modern scenario we translate all
    399 +        assets so the centroid lands near Kyiv when the dataset has not been
    400 +        migrated yet.
    401 +        """
    402 +
    403 +        dataset_root = Path(self.data_in).expanduser()
    404 +        sentinel = dataset_root / '.ukraine_localized'
    405 +        waypoints_path = (dataset_root / self.waypoints).expanduser()
    406 +        if sentinel.exists() or not waypoints_path.exists():
    407 +            return
    408 +        current_center = self._compute_waypoint_centroid(waypoints_path)
    409 +        if current_center is None:
    410 +            return
    411 +        target_center = (32.0, 49.0)
    412 +        delta_lon = target_center[0] - current_center[0]
    413 +        delta_lat = target_center[1] - current_center[1]
    414 +        if abs(delta_lon) < 0.05 and abs(delta_lat) < 0.05:
    415 +            sentinel.write_text('already localized', encoding='utf-8')
    416 +            return
    417 +        logger.info('Recentering flight clone dataset by Δlon=%s Δlat=%s',
    418 +            round(delta_lon, 4), round(delta_lat, 4))
    419 +        self._shift_waypoints_file(waypoints_path, delta_lon, delta_lat)
    420 +        for csv_name in ('beams.csv', 'satellites.csv'):
    421 +            csv_path = dataset_root / csv_name
    422 +            if csv_path.exists():
    423 +                self._shift_csv_coordinates(csv_path, delta_lon, delta_lat)
    424 +        sentinel.write_text('ukraine', encoding='utf-8')
    425 +
    426 +    def _compute_waypoint_centroid(self, path: Path
    427 +        ) ->tuple[float, float] | None:
    428 +        try:
    429 +            payload = json.loads(path.read_text(encoding='utf-8'))
    430 +        except Exception as exc:
    431 +            logger.warning('Unable to read %s: %s', path, exc)
    432 +            return None
    433 +        total_lon = 0.0
    434 +        total_lat = 0.0
    435 +        samples = 0
    436 +        for feature in payload.get('features', []):
    437 +            geometry = feature.get('geometry') or {}
    438 +            coordinates = geometry.get('coordinates') or []
    439 +            if not coordinates:
    440 +                continue
    441 +            sequence = coordinates[0] if isinstance(coordinates[0][0],
    442 +                list) else coordinates
    443 +            for entry in sequence:
    444 +                if len(entry) < 2:
    445 +                    continue
    446 +                try:
    447 +                    total_lon += float(entry[0])
    448 +                    total_lat += float(entry[1])
    449 +                    samples += 1
    450 +                except (TypeError, ValueError):
    451 +                    continue
    452 +        if not samples:
    453 +            return None
    454 +        return total_lon / samples, total_lat / samples
    455 +
    456 +    def _shift_waypoints_file(self, path: Path, delta_lon: float,
    457 +        delta_lat: float) ->None:
    458 +        payload = json.loads(path.read_text(encoding='utf-8'))
    459 +        for feature in payload.get('features', []):
    460 +            geometry = feature.get('geometry') or {}
    461 +            coordinates = geometry.get('coordinates') or []
    462 +            if not coordinates:
    463 +                continue
    464 +            nested = isinstance(coordinates[0][0], list)
    465 +            sequence = coordinates[0] if nested else coordinates
    466 +            for entry in sequence:
    467 +                if len(entry) >= 2:
    468 +                    entry[0] = float(entry[0]) + delta_lon
    469 +                    entry[1] = float(entry[1]) + delta_lat
    470 +            if nested:
    471 +                geometry['coordinates'] = [sequence]
    472 +            else:
    473 +                geometry['coordinates'] = sequence
    474 +        path.write_text(json.dumps(payload, indent=2), encoding='utf-8')
    475 +
    476 +    def _shift_csv_coordinates(self, path: Path, delta_lon: float,
    477 +        delta_lat: float) ->None:
    478 +        try:
    479 +            if path.name == 'beams.csv':
    480 +                df = pd.read_csv(path, header=None, names=['beam', 'lon',
    481 +                    'lat'])
    482 +                df['lon'] = df['lon'].astype(float) + delta_lon
    483 +                df['lat'] = df['lat'].astype(float) + delta_lat
    484 +                df.to_csv(path, header=False, index=False)
    485 +            else:
    486 +                df = pd.read_csv(path)
    487 +                if 'beam_long' in df.columns:
    488 +                    df['beam_long'] = df['beam_long'].astype(float) + delta_lon
    489 +                if 'beam_lat' in df.columns:
    490 +                    df['beam_lat'] = df['beam_lat'].astype(float) + delta_lat
    491 +                df.to_csv(path, index=False)
    492 +        except Exception as exc:
    493 +            logger.warning('Unable to shift %s: %s', path, exc)
    494 +
    495      def _prepare_waypoint_files(self, *, features: Iterable[dict[str, Any]],

    19 +- The cloning workflow now recenters every dataset over Ukraine (Kyiv → Dnipro/Lviv/Odesa). The manager renormalises `waypoints.geojson`, `beams.csv`, and `satellites.csv` once per dataset and drops a `.ukraine_localized` marker so subsequent runs keep your manual tweaks intact.
